Pudong Residents Resolutely Oppose Moving the Xidu Wharf; Original Ferry Landing Is Allowed to Be Encroached and Merged by Asiatic Petroleum; Over a Hundred Residents Hold Farm Tools to Resist Work; - Yesterday, the Situation of Confrontation Between the Two Sides Was Serious - 161

The Municipal Public Works Bureau's recent relocation of the Xidu Wharf in Pudong and the allowing of the original ferry landing to be encroached and merged by the British Asiatic Petroleum Company has aroused strong opposition from local residents. However, the road to the old ferry landing has been blocked off by construction workers since the 24th, causing great alarm among the residents. On that day, more than 100 women from Chenjiazhai, Majiazhai, Taojiayan, and Yujia gathered nearby, each wielding long and short farm tools, to block the construction, preventing it from proceeding. For the past two days, they have continued to resist the workers, and the two sides have been in a stalemate, with the situation being quite serious. Yesterday, local citizens elected representatives Jia Jinfang, Pan Bosheng, and others to submit a report to the Pudong Native Place Association, requesting assistance and advocating for the benefit of transportation. The original text is recorded below:

"To Whom It May Concern: The Municipal Public Works Bureau is developing a municipal ferry plan and relocating the Xidu Wharf. We have repeatedly petitioned and forwarded requests to the Municipal Government to allow the preservation of the original road for the benefit of the people. We previously received a copy of the Shanghai Municipal Government's No. 1339 approval from your association, stating that there is still space next to the newly built Xidu pontoon wharf that can be used by the public and can also solve the water extraction problem, etc. After examining the meaning of the approval, it seems that the original road is to be abandoned, which is very alarming to us. Recently, we saw a joint notice issued by the Shanghai Municipal Public Works Bureau stating: 'Regarding the case of the Municipal Ferry moving the Xidu Wharf, Pudong citizens have stated that the elimination of the old wharf will cause some inconvenience for water extraction and unloading. They have requested that another wharf be opened to facilitate transportation. This Bureau has surveyed the area east of the Asiatic Petroleum wharf to the Hefeng Factory and found that there is no small road leading to it. It is not easy to open a new wharf. However, there is still vacant land next to the newly built ferry at Xidu. A request has been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval to allocate funds for this Public Works Bureau to build a public wharf for the public to extract water and unload goods. All citizens must not cause further disturbances to the Asiatic Petroleum Company's construction work at the old wharf at Xidu. In addition to setting up civil signs at the site of the public wharf to be built at the Xidu Wharf to clarify the boundaries and prepare for construction, this notice is hereby issued to make it known, etc.' We believe that the road that we have repeatedly requested to preserve for the convenience of transportation will soon be blocked off, and there is no way to appeal. We must once again appeal to your association (1). It is not easy to find a road leading to the wharf between the boundary of the Hefeng Factory and Asiatic Petroleum. This road should be ceded by Asiatic Petroleum. Moreover, there was an eight-foot-wide road before the Xipu Road. If the foreign merchant refuses to cede it, then they should not be allowed to encroach and merge the Xidu Wharf. Furthermore, there are precedents for municipal ferry wharves that are separated by roads and use pontoons for transportation, such as the Hongsheng Wharf of the Laiyi Ferry in Pudong, which is separated by the Duijiang Ferry Road, and the Gonghexing Wharf of the public ferry in Hongkou, the Public Concession, which is separated by Zhaofeng Road. Why should Asiatic Petroleum be allowed to be different? Moreover, the municipal government has long had a ban on allowing oil storage to be built, except for Gaoqiao Sand. The central area along the Pu River has long been banned. How can Asiatic Petroleum be allowed to expand again? (2) Since the Municipal Ferry Wharf has been built on Xipu Road, how can the wharf that the public is used to be demolished and taken away without leaving anything behind? After repeated efforts, a public announcement has been issued, stating that a public wharf for the public will be built later to satisfy the citizens. However, suddenly offering the Xidu Wharf to others for encroachment and obstruction does not conform to the eighth article of the National Construction Outline, which is to repair roads, develop transportation, and benefit the people, as taught by President Sun. We have grown up here and our interests are intertwined. For the sake of transportation and the prosperity of the municipality, it is difficult to remain silent. Therefore, we have prepared this document and submitted it to your association for review. We earnestly request your strong assistance and advocate for the preservation of the ferry landing and the benefit of transportation, which is indeed very inconvenient. Sincerely submitted."

Current Status of Radio in Our Country; Over Thirty Radio Stations Have Been Built in Various Provinces and Cities; Communication Has Been Established with the United States, Russia, France, the Netherlands, Germany, and Other Countries; Communication in the Border Provinces Is Currently Being Prepared 162

The Ministry of Communications believes that radio has a wide range of uses, and in recent years, it has been expanding domestic radio station installations and international communication efforts without sparing any effort. The recent status of domestic and international radio communication is summarized below:

Survey of Domestic Radio Stations 163

The provinces that have established radio stations include: (Jiangsu) Shanghai, Nanjing, Chongming, Qidong; (Zhejiang) Hangzhou, Dinghai, Ningbo, Kanmen, Shenshan; (Jiangxi) Nanchang; (Henan) Zhengzhou, Luoyang; (Anhui) Wuhu, Anqing (now abolished); (Shandong) Jinan, Qingdao, Yantai, Weihaiwei; (Hubei) Hankou, Shashi, Yichang, Wuchang; (Hebei) Beiping, Tianjin; (Hunan) Changsha; (Yunnan) Kunming (can relay to all parts of Yunnan Province), Macau; (Sichuan) Chongqing, Chengdu, Wanxian, Xufu. These four stations can relay to all parts of Sichuan Province; (Guangdong and Guangxi) Guangzhou, Shantou, can relay to all parts of Guangdong and Guangxi Provinces; (Fujian) Fuzhou, Xiamen; (Guizhou) Guiyang (can relay to all parts of Guizhou Province).

Preparations in the Border Areas 164

As for the border provinces, such as Xinjiang, Tibet, and Qinghai, the only means of communication currently relied upon is military radio stations, and the equipment for commercial radio stations is still lacking. In order to complete the national radio route plan and develop the culture and commerce of the border regions, the Ministry of Communications recruited more than 20 telegraph operators willing to serve in the border regions and sent them off last month to prepare everything in Xinjiang. They have now arrived in Dihua, the provincial capital, but due to political disputes in the province, they have been unable to implement the original plan. Once the province returns to normal, formal communication can begin. Active preparations are also underway in Tibet and Qinghai, and communication should be realized in succession soon.

A Glimpse of International Communication 165

The Ministry of Communications believes that international radio communication has a close relationship with the increase in understanding and friendship between countries and the development of commerce. Therefore, it has actively pursued communication with various countries. Formal communication has now been established with the United States, Russia, France, the Netherlands, and Germany. As for the planned Sino-American communication, the construction of new telegraph stations, antenna towers, and other projects in Zhenru has been completed in succession. Two transmitters ordered from England have been shipped to Shanghai, one of which has been installed and debugged. The other one can also arrive in Shanghai for installation this month. Therefore, formal communication can be implemented within this year.

Establishment of a Telecommunications Manufacturing Plant 166

It is reported that after the dissolution of the Telecommunications Manufacturing Plant by the Ministry of Communications, the supply of electrical materials for various provinces in the country is being manufactured by the Electrical Machinery Manufacturing Plant of the Construction Commission. However, all of its products are in short supply. The Ministry of Communications is now planning to establish a telecommunications manufacturing plant in Shanghai to remedy the situation. All plans have been completed, and it can be opened soon once funding is secured. On the one hand, in order to save expenses, it has specially purchased a generator from the Construction Committee, and is currently building houses in Zhengu to prepare for its installation. In the future, part of the electricity needed by the radio station will be supplied by the generator.

Newly Arrived Overseas Chinese in Shanghai Suspected of Being Communists; Public Safety Bureau Fails to Provide Evidence; Special Court Still Does Not Transfer Them; - Dispute Over Jurisdiction Arises - 167

Chen Yuxiu, Xie Xinming, Xu Jian, and Xie Zuoyu, overseas Chinese who arrived in Shanghai from Southeast Asia for business less than two months ago, were recently suspected of being communists by the Shanghai Municipal Public Safety Bureau. At 10:55 pm on the 18th of this month, police were led to No. 5, Continental New Village, Scott Road, to carry out the arrest. However, the Des Voeux Road Police Station detained the four men and sent them to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court because the area was under the jurisdiction of the Municipal Council. Because the Public Safety Bureau requested the transfer of the case but did not provide any evidence, the court ordered a postponement and instructed the Public Safety Bureau to submit evidence for further verification. The four defendants were each allowed to post a bail of 500 yuan, as previously reported in detail. Yesterday morning, Yu Hua, the chief of the criminal division of the Second High Court, along with two judges, Zhou and Jiang, opened a criminal court to continue the hearing. The police station was represented by lawyers Li Zhishan and Gan Jingchong, the Public Safety Bureau was represented by legal advisor Lawyer Zhan Jifeng, and the defendants were represented by Lawyer Yue Junfen. First, Judge Yu asked the defendants when they moved into Continental New Village. According to Chen Yuxiu's reply, the house originally belonged to a woman named Chen Liuxiang, who transferred it to us on September 1, and he presented a receipt for the transfer fee as proof. Next, the inspector of the Public Safety Bureau claimed that the four defendants were indeed communists and that the evidence was all in the Chinese area, so he requested permission to transfer them. Lawyer Zhan Jifeng proposed that the primary question in this case was whether the court had jurisdiction, because the defendants' place of residence was in the Chinese area and the construction of the house was licensed by the Municipal Public Works Bureau. Therefore, the jurisdictional question should be resolved. Lawyer Li Zhishan immediately stated that if the defendants were indeed communists, the police station would be happy to assist, but this case had been postponed for a week and there was still no evidence submitted. The names of the defendants were not included in the list submitted last time, and even today, they are still claiming it is a piece of order and have no other evidence. As for the jurisdictional question raised by the Public Safety Bureau, since this case has been accepted by this court, it is already under the jurisdiction of this court. The Criminal Procedure Law stipulates that the arrest of a criminal must be carried out with an arrest warrant issued by the court, stating the age, origin, and characteristics of the person being arrested. Today, the Public Safety Bureau has failed to provide this procedure and has no evidence to submit. Therefore, we request the court to rule that the transfer is not allowed. Lawyer Zhan replied that since the defendants' residence was in the Chinese area, the Public Safety Bureau could arrest them without notifying the police station. As for the arrest warrant issue, the police station often arrests criminals in the Chinese area without a court arrest warrant, and the Public Safety Bureau has always assisted them without objection. The police station's raising of this point is actually nitpicking. The defendants' lawyer then presented multiple letters from the Batavia General Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to prove that the defendants were legitimate businessmen who had come to Shanghai to do business. Finally, Lawyer Li from the police station and Lawyer Zhan from the Public Safety Bureau argued for a long time over the jurisdiction and evidence issues. Lawyer Zhan solemnly declared that jurisdiction was the primary question in this case. Before this question could be resolved, he requested that the case be postponed for one week so that the Public Safety Bureau could gather evidence and submit a proposal. The court granted the request and ordered the case to be postponed for another hearing. The defendants were still released on the original bail.

Zhu Baoyuan's Death Leaves Behind a Huge Fortune, Causing Endless Family Turmoil; Zhu Ziyan, Qingshun, and Qing'ai Love Money More Than Flesh and Blood; After the Sisters' Lawsuit Was Settled, the Stepmother Sued the Court Again; - Not Afraid of Poverty, but Afraid of Unevenness; Poor Inheritance System - 168

Zhenhe Tea Shop owner Zhu Baoyuan came from humble beginnings and became wealthy through business. His legacy of nearly three million was all in the hands of his two sons, Zhu Yanqing and Zhu Shunqing. However, these two brothers only cared about money and did not cherish their family. Even their biological sisters and their late father's stepmother were unwilling to give them a legal share, causing his two married sisters to feel resentful and file a lawsuit for division of property in the summer. Yanqing and others then hurriedly sought mediation, broke their stingy pockets slightly, and the lawsuit was settled. Unexpectedly, one wave had just subsided, and another wave arose. Now, his stepmother, Zhu Xinxinbao, is also suing the First Special District District Court, alleging that she has been deprived of property, etc. As the saying goes, "Not afraid of poverty, but afraid of unevenness." Zhu's two sons did not share their father's wealth with their family, which caused the litigation to be repeatedly initiated. Although it is due to the poor inheritance system, it is also due to improper handling. The story of Zhu's rise and the origin of this mother-son lawsuit are described below, based on the interviews:

Current Situation of the Zhu Family 169

Zhu Baoyuan, a native of Haining, Zhejiang, died of illness at his residence in Shanghai on April 27 of this year. He left behind two sons, the eldest Yanqing and the second Shunqing, and three daughters, all born to his previous wife. He remarried Xi Xinbao, who is now only 33 years old and a native of Wuxian. She was married on December 16, 1930, and has not yet had any children. The three daughters born to his previous wife have already had two daughters married, but the youngest is still unmarried. Yanqing's brothers have all been married and have children. Shunqing also took a concubine, the famous prostitute Paper Tent Plum Blossom Lao Jiu. Later, his wife Mao died of typhoid fever, and Jiu was promoted to take charge of the kitchen. The Zhenhe Tea Shop opened by Baoyuan is located at No. 133, Lane 6, De'anli, North Shanxi Road. It has been a long time since its establishment. In addition to the tea shop, the types of inheritance are complicated, and the amount of property totals more than 2.7 million. It is not easy to achieve this result after starting from scratch.

From Poverty to Prosperity in Shanghai 170

Zhu's family was originally very poor. When Baoyuan was 15 or 16 years old, he was still a peddler in his hometown. He carried a basket all day long, walking back and forth on the streets, selling water chestnuts and fruits to make a living. One autumn tide season, wealthy merchants from Shanghai came to Haining to watch the tide. Baoyuan suddenly found a wallet at the tide-watching spot, which he thought was lost by a visitor. He sat there waiting for the owner to return it. After a while, the owner came and saw the wallet placed in his basket. Baoyuan offered it back without being asked. The guest offered him money, but he refused. The guest was so grateful that he brought him to Shanghai to find a job. Unexpectedly, after arriving in Shanghai, the person suddenly received an urgent telegram calling him back, so he left Baoyuan in a teahouse in Xiaobeimen. Deng You, the owner of the Pi Zou Yinji Wood Shop, visited the teahouse every three days to taste tea. He saw Baoyuan looking distressed, was surprised, and questioned him. After hearing the whole story, he not only pitied his drifting and helpless situation, but also admired his sincerity and integrity as a young man, and knew that he was not someone who would be content with his current circumstances. So, he took him home and introduced him to work in a small money shop nearby. This was the beginning of Baoyuan's entry into the business world. The money shop was near a tea shop. At that time, the tea shop had to rely on translators to communicate with foreign firms when selling tea. They were called "interpreters." The interpreter of the tea shop, surnamed Han, gradually became acquainted with Baoyuan because he admired his sincerity and appreciated his knowledge. In his spare time, he taught him English, and Baoyuan was also blessed with intelligence. Therefore, Han became more fond of him and listed him as a student. His career improved step by step. After several years, he used his savings to marry a woman from Huzhou. Yanqing's brothers and sisters were born to this woman. Soon after, he raised funds to open the Zhenhe Tea Shop, and from then on, everything went smoothly. In addition, he was good at socializing, so he was sure to win. He earned huge profits every year, and Zhenhe changed from a partnership to a sole proprietorship, which remains to this day.

Anecdotes from His Remarriage 171

After Baoyuan became wealthy, his desire for women arose spontaneously. Although he was naturally stingy and enjoyed eating leftovers, he had almost every request fulfilled for women. In the past, there was a prostitute named Bai Chongming Lao Er on Shantou Road who was greatly favored by Baoyuan. When she was mourning the death of her husband, Lao Er once asked to make a vow of lifelong commitment. Later, because his son Shunqing took Paper Tent Plum Blossom Lao Jiu as a concubine, and Er Jiu had some relationship, he parted with Er and hired Xi Xinbao as his successor. On the day of the wedding, Lao Er was deeply resentful of Baoyuan's betrayal and broke into the hall, causing a great wave of jealousy. Those who participated in the grand ceremony that day, even though it has been several years, still clap their hands and laugh when they mention the past, citing it as a rare and interesting drama.

The Sisters' Lawsuit 172

Zhu Baoyuan's three daughters, born to his first wife, other than the youngest daughter who is still unmarried, the eldest daughter, Zhu Jun, is 31 years old and married to the Shi family. She lives at No. 33, Puyutang Street. The second daughter, Zhu Meizhen, is 21 years old and married to the Wang family. She now lives at No. 12, Shenyuli, Tiantong Road. The husbands of the two daughters are quite wealthy and self-sufficient. Therefore, after Baoyuan's death, they knew that according to current law, married daughters still have the right to inherit their parents' property. Out of consideration for their siblings' feelings, they did not want to immediately dispute with their two brothers. However, they saw Yanqing and Shunqing colluding with each other, intending to swallow all of the 2.7 million inheritance. They resented their arrogance and excessive deception, so they jointly filed a lawsuit for division of property as a warning to promote their awakening. Yanqing's brothers knew that they were in the wrong and feared that they would fail if the law was used to judge them. Therefore, they tried to mediate in every possible way. The two sisters believed that they seemed to have repented, so they did not go too far. They abandoned their inheritance rights, accepted the mediator's proposal, each received 80,000 yuan, and submitted a statement to withdraw the lawsuit. Therefore, the case was only heard in court once and then there was no news.

Mother and Son Lawsuit Opens Again 173

The late Zhu Baoyuan's second wife, Xi Xinbao, a native of Dongting Mountain, although childless after marrying Baoyuan, treated his two sons and three daughters from his first marriage as her own. Now, because the two sons, Yanjing and Shunqing, did not legally distribute all of the inheritance, she has retained lawyer Chen Ying to file a lawsuit, stating that, according to Article 1138, Paragraph 1, and Article 1144, Paragraph 1 of the Inheritance Section of the Civil Code, it should be divided equally into six shares (referring to Zhu's two sons, three daughters, and the plaintiff). The two married daughters have voluntarily relinquished their rights, settling for 80,000 yuan each. The defendants, seeing the successful employment of the "bitter meat stratagem", in an instant, have gained an undue benefit of over 700,000 yuan. They consider this the only surefire way to make an unearned profit, while completely disregarding the unmarried younger sister and the widowed stepmother, placing them in a state of neglect. The brothers competed for the estate with public accusations in the newspapers, but it eventually died down, followed by a secret agreement for division, the circumstances of which are difficult to describe. The plaintiff believes that the true state of the inheritance should be made public, and all important account books, land deeds, property deeds, various stocks, public bonds, and other valuable securities owned by her late husband during his lifetime are kept by the defendants in the tea shop. After her lawyer sent a letter requesting access to them, they ignored it, repeatedly offering reconciliation as a delaying tactic. First, they offered 120,000 yuan, then 200,000 yuan, but consistently refused to hand over the account books, with the intention of using the delay to fabricate or tamper with evidence, or to destroy evidence in order to conceal or alter the existing inheritance. It is now rumored that a portion of the inheritance has already been stolen and sold. The share of the unmarried minor daughter could have been claimed by the plaintiff in her capacity as guardian or stepmother. However, to demonstrate her transparency, she is only defending herself, leaving others to take their own course and not wanting to interfere and cause further disputes. Out of the existing 2.7 million yuan, after deducting 80,000 yuan for each of the married daughters, there remains over 2.54 million yuan. If the plaintiff, two sons, and one daughter divide this equally, the plaintiff should receive over 635,000 yuan. She respectfully requests the court to promptly order the defendants to pay this amount to protect her legal rights and private property.

Application for Litigation Aid 174

After the plaintiff, Zhu Xi Xinbao, filed the lawsuit, the litigation costs, based on the subject matter, were approximately 3,120 yuan. As she has been living in difficult circumstances since her husband's death, she is unable to afford such a large sum. Therefore, her representative lawyer, Chen Ying, applied for litigation aid according to Article 107 of the Civil Procedure Law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qiao Wanxuan of the First Special Court held a hearing on this matter. Lawyer Chen Ying stated the reasons why the plaintiff was unable to raise the litigation costs and requested a temporary exemption. If a guarantor was needed, he could provide one. However, the defendant's lawyer expressed opposition, saying that the plaintiff had private savings and was not impoverished. Lawyer Chen responded that the decision to grant litigation aid was up to the judge and could not be objected to by the opposing party. After debate between the two lawyers, Judge Qiao ordered the plaintiff to provide a guarantee according to regulations and await a decision.

Two Doctors, Absurdly Promising a Cure and Causing a Death; Yao Hongsheng Died from Excessive Bleeding After Surgery; the Two Doctors Fled in Fear of Punishment After Causing the Tragedy 175

Yao Ye Shi, an old woman from Shaoxing, residing in a rented room at 210 Xin Xin Li, Jin Shenfu Road, French Concession, is 62 years old. She works as an "amah" (nursemaid) in Western households. Her son, Yao Hongsheng, is 33 years old and works as a clerk at the Eastern Huili Bank on the Bund. His first wife has passed away, and he has two sons and a second wife, Wan, from his hometown. In May of this year, Yao Hongsheng suddenly suffered from stomach pains. He consulted Dr. Niu Huilin, who cured the stomach ailment, but then a lump appeared on his left shoulder blade, causing redness and extreme pain. He consulted both Chinese and Western doctors without success. As time went on, the lump gradually swelled, becoming as large as a bowl, with internal ulceration but no pus. In Chinese surgical terms, this condition is called "Shang Da Shou," also known as a type of "Zheng." A few days ago, a neighbor, Hu Zuoquan, who works as a chief clerk, introduced him to two Western doctors from the Xin Xin Hospital at 66 Xin Xin Li, near his residence: Xu Hongbin and Zhu Xianchu, both from Haimen. They agreed on a medical fee of 50 yuan, with half paid in advance. Doctors Xu and Zhu jointly issued a guarantee, promising a full recovery within 40 days. The guarantee also stipulated that after recovery, in addition to paying the remaining half of the medical fee, a commemorative plaque would be presented. After completing these formalities, the doctors ordered Yao Hongsheng to return home, where the doctors would come to his house for daily treatment. On the 25th, at around 10 a.m., Doctors Xu and Zhu brought a surgical kit to Yao's house, ordering Hongsheng to lie face down on the bed, where they performed surgery to cut and treat the affected area. Unexpectedly, Hongsheng had been suffering from the illness for a long time, and his body was extremely weak. Due to excessive bleeding after the surgery, he became delirious and was on the verge of death. The two doctors were frightened by the situation, realizing their lack of medical expertise and experience had caused the tragedy. They ordered his family to hire someone to take Hongsheng to Guangci Hospital for treatment, while the two doctors went to Guangci Hospital to make arrangements. However, before Hongsheng could be treated after being carried to the entrance of Guangci Hospital, he breathed his last and died. His family immediately sought out the two doctors, Xu and Zhu, for an explanation. However, the two doctors had already fled out of guilt. The deceased's mother then had the body transported back home and reported the incident to the French police station for investigation. The police chief sent detectives to Xin Xin Hospital, but Doctors Xu and Zhu had already fled and could not be arrested. Yesterday morning, the police station reported to the Second Special District Court, which appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with a forensic doctor and clerk, to inspect Yao's home. Due to insufficient lighting in the house and unclear external examination of the affected area of the body, an autopsy was required. The body was then sent to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Autopsy Center. At 2:30 p.m., Prosecutor Wang, accompanied by forensic doctors Wei and Jiang, arrived at the center and performed an autopsy on the affected area of the body. The judge then took the bench and questioned the deceased's mother, wife, and the introducer, Hu Zuoquan. It was ruled that Yao Hongsheng died from excessive bleeding after surgery for a soft tissue tumor. The body was released to the family, Yao Ye Shi, etc., for burial. The doctors who performed the surgery, Xu Hongbin, etc., were deemed to have been negligent in their duties and should be investigated and dealt with by the police department. After the autopsy, the police prepared a coffin for the body and launched a search for the two doctors who had fled, to bring them to justice for interrogation.

Public Concession Physician Registry to Publish Fourth Edition 180

Since 1931, the Public Works Bureau has conducted voluntary registration for physicians, dentists, and veterinarians within the Concession. Since its inception, the registry has been published in three editions, and the number of registrants has gradually increased. There are now over 800 registrants. The Public Works Bureau plans to publish the fourth edition of the registry. For the sake of completeness, those who have already registered should contact the registration director at Office No. 210 in the Public Works Bureau regarding any changes, or those who have not yet registered and wish to do so should begin the registration process. Any physician, dentist, or veterinarian whose name appears in the registry is evidence that they have registered with the Public Works Bureau and been recognized by the Shanghai Medical Affairs Committee. If a name does not appear in the registry, it is evidence of non-registration. Physicians who wish to register, and registered individuals who wish to make changes to their registry, must contact the bureau immediately.

Lieutenant Hall Apprehended on the Jinpu Railway, American Prosecutor Flies to Tianjin to Investigate 181

Further Hearing in Qian Shaofeng's Father Revenge Case 182

He Zunfu, a 35-year-old man from Guizhou, previously served in the military and political circles. Recently unemployed, he came to Shanghai with his servant, Tian Guixiang, in August, and stayed in Room 33 of the Datong Apartment in the Daodeli, Beile Road, French Concession. On the evening of the 16th of this month, He and his friend, Li Yanyan, went to see a movie at the Golden Grand Theatre in the Eight Immortals Bridge. At around 10 p.m., he was suddenly stabbed in the abdomen by a knife in the theater. The assailant fled to the entrance and was captured. After interrogation by the police, the assailant confessed his name as Qian Shaofeng, styled Peigao, 20 years old, from Guizhou, and stated that he was taking revenge for his father. The police immediately sent He to Renji Hospital for treatment and escorted Qian to the Second Special District Court for questioning and detention, pending He's recovery. Later, He died due to his injuries. The body was reported to the court, which sent personnel to verify it. His servant telegraphed He Rong, the deceased's son who was studying at the Nanjing Military Academy, to come to Shanghai to arrange for burial. This was reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday morning, Judge Wang Gangxu of the criminal court convened witnesses and ordered the defendant to be brought to court for further hearing in the Criminal Court No. 1. The police lawyer stated that the victim in this case had died due to his injuries, and the police were changing the charge against the defendant to premeditated murder under Article 284, Paragraph 1, Clause 1 of the Criminal Code, and requested that the defendant be tried accordingly. During questioning, the defendant Qian Shaofeng stated: "In the early spring of 1929, as I was about to get married, He Zunfu, the magistrate of An'nan County, Guizhou, unreasonably extorted my father, Qian Bin, forcing him to borrow 1,000 taels of silver and 400 taels of opium. My father had served in various positions, including the Finance Bureau, the Militia Bureau, the Educational Bureau, and as a primary school principal. He had always been honest and had no assets, so he refused to comply. He then held a grudge and colluded with Zhou Haitao, the company commander stationed in the county, who led a team on the night of the 5th day of the third lunar month of that year to arrest my father. The next morning, he was executed by shooting for "various unlawful acts and defiance of orders." Under their evil influence, I had no way to file a lawsuit. After my marriage, I vowed to take revenge. I tearfully said goodbye to my elderly mother and wife and went to Wuhan to study. Due to a flood, I transferred to Sanmin School in Nanjing. After the September 18th Incident, I joined the school's volunteer army. After going north, I entered Datong University in Beiping. Later, I received a letter from home stating that my hometown had suffered years of famine and was unable to provide tuition fees. I came to Shanghai in January of last year and entered the China Wireless Electric Engineering School. After graduation, I never stopped thinking about avenging my father's death. Earlier this month, I met He near the Datong Apartment on Edward Road. Seeing him enter the Datong Apartment, I learned that He had been living in the apartment for a long time. I then purchased a sharp weapon and waited for an opportunity. On the night of the 16th, I saw He go out and followed him. Seeing him enter the movie theater, I did not buy a ticket to enter and sat in the back row close to He, waiting for a chance to strike and wound my enemy. I stabbed him several times. I cannot remember how many times because I was in a state of mental confusion." When asked how he knew He Zunfu was his enemy, Qian replied, "After my father's death, He sent someone to notify us, telling us not to publicize the matter, otherwise it would be detrimental to my entire family. Everyone in my hometown knows about this." At this point, as the victim's son had not arrived, the official questioned the witnesses Li Yanyan and the two police officers who arrested Qian about the situation at the time. The official then ordered a letter to be sent to the An'nan County government in Guizhou to investigate the case and set a date for further hearing.

Daring to Steal and Sell Part of a Rented Shipyard Building - Zhang Jianfei Sues Fang Jianan and Others 186

Zhang has now discovered that Fang and others have privately sold a building in Baota Bay, Yangzhou, to Feng Jinhai, and divided the proceeds among themselves. Zhang believes that after the lease expires, it must be returned to the Zhejiang Construction Department, and if any of the leased items are missing, it will be difficult to avoid responsibility. It was only recently discovered by me, and the buyer has already rebuilt the old house into a new one. However, when my lease expires and I return it to the Construction Department, they must inspect the leased items according to the agreement. Therefore, I had no choice but to negotiate with the defendants. Since this incident occurred, Zhuo Binghou has fled. The Yangzhou branch is now managed by a person surnamed Zhang. Judge Xiao stated that the case still required investigation and ordered the plaintiff to await further review.

Chief of Anti-Smuggling District Sentenced for Colluding with Brother in Smuggling Salt 193

Pan Baozhong, the chief of the anti-smuggling district, colluded with his younger brother, Pan Axiang, a well-known salt smuggler, during his tenure, to smuggle a large amount of contraband salt. His captain, Zhou Yufeng, led the salt ships into Zhangyan Estuary, where they were intercepted by the local salt police. Salt smugglers Zhang Shengkuan and others opened fire to resist arrest, resulting in a fierce battle in which two salt police officers were killed. The military police apprehended Zhang Shengkuan, Zhou Yufeng, Pan Jubao, and Zhou Jiafu, and handed them over to the authorities. They were transferred to the Shanghai District Court, where Prosecutor Yang ordered Pan Baozhong to be summoned and detained, and jointly prosecuted. After repeated investigations by the criminal court, the facts were clarified, and after the closing arguments, Judge Guan opened the court yesterday to pronounce the sentence. Zhang Shengkuan was found guilty of salt smuggling and homicide, and sentenced to life imprisonment. Pan Baozhong and Zhou Yufeng were each sentenced to ten years of imprisonment for conspiracy to smuggle more than 3,000 catties of salt while resisting arrest with weapons. Pan Jubao and Zhou Jiafu were found not guilty. The trial of Xiao Shizhang, Zhou Zhencai, Han Sanbao, Xiao A'san, and Pan Axiang was suspended pending their arrest. Pan Baozhong and others declared their dissatisfaction in court, and the court granted them the right to appeal.

Minutes of the Standing Committee Meeting of the National Lichia Association 198

The Chinese National Lichia Federation held its 22nd Standing Committee meeting yesterday, chaired by Zhang Yichen. Discussions included: (1) A letter from the government of Shuyang County, Jiangsu Province, regarding the occupation of property belonging to the Gongshantang Public Hall, which has been investigated and handled. It was decided to forward the matter to the Public Hall. (2) A letter from the Zhishantang Public Hall in Xiazhen, Shandong, requesting the issuance of promotional materials. It was decided to refer it to the Propaganda Department. (3) A letter from the Xuzhou Lichia Association regarding disruptions affecting the association's affairs. It was decided to assign personnel from the Organization Department to reorganize it. (4) A letter from the Wuxi Lichia Association in Jiangsu, forwarded from the Jingjiang Pushantang Public Hall, recommending Liu Yunbo as the leader. It was decided to approve it. (5) A letter from the Yishantang Public Hall in Weixian, Shandong, requesting the issuance of certificates and badges. It was decided to reply by letter. (6) A letter from the Renshantang Public Hall in Yuci, Shanxi, requesting the protection of the authorities for a scheduled general meeting. It was decided to approve it. (7) A letter from the director of the Dongcheng Shanzantang Public Hall in Jiangyin, Jiangsu, regarding attacks against the director. It was decided to reply by letter, as the individual had voluntarily requested withdrawal. (8) A letter from the Chengxintang Public Hall in Bengbu, Anhui, requesting the issuance of certificates. It was decided to reply by letter. (9) A letter from the Yushantang Public Hall in Shouyi, Shanxi, regarding a proposed change to a branch association. It was decided that it should remain a public hall to conform to the naming convention. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

A fire broke out suddenly at 8:50 AM yesterday at the Guangdong Brothers Rubber Company factory at No. 470 Peikai'er Road in East Shanghai. The fire was very intense. The fire brigade responded and extinguished the fire. The reported loss is several hundred taels of silver.

City Voices 200

Recent News from the Zhenxing Woolen Mill: The "Snow Shame" soft wool fabric produced by the Zhenxing Woolen Textile Factory on Xujiahui Road in this city has elasticity and is comparable to Vienna imports in every aspect, while its price is less than one-third of the imported product. Its colors are also permanent and do not fade. It is suitable for making autumn suits and winter shirts. It is also reported that the "Double Dragon" brand of various four-strand and six-strand wool threads produced by the factory is a leader among domestic wool yarn products. Since its launch, it has spread throughout the country. The factory has a retail store in the Penglai Market, and recent cold weather has made it even more crowded with shoppers.

▲ Additional Classes and Professors at the Banking Practicum: The Banking Practicum on the second floor of the Jingbao Newspaper Building on Wangping Street, Sima Road, began classes on the 21st. Therefore, to meet the urgent need for banking talent and assist students, in addition to the original schedule, two additional classes have been added from 8:30 AM to 10:30 AM and from 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM, open to both men and women. Everything remains as before. Banking knowledge is urgently needed in society, and this practicum is a rare opportunity. Those who are interested should not miss this opportunity. Registration is open for immediate classes. Out-of-town requests for correspondence courses have been received, so the practicum has added a correspondence course to promote widespread learning. Please include postage for brochures. Tuition fees for those introduced by banks will be appropriately reduced.

Medical News 201

▲ Dr. Zhao Xiaosong's Clinic Adds Throat Department: Dr. Zhao Xiaosong's clinic at No. 17 Taiyuan Lane, east of the Great World, has recently added a throat department due to the prevalence of throat ailments. Dr. Liu Boming, a throat specialist from the capital, has been invited to Shanghai to provide consultations. Shanghai Hospital Expands Ward Facilities: Since its establishment, the Shanghai Hospital on both roads has been receiving an increasing number of patients. Recently, clinics along the line have been sending patients who require hospitalization to the Shanghai Hospital. However, the hospital only has 25 beds, which is insufficient. The Health Section plans to add eight beds in the vacant room on the fourth floor of the hospital, where the radio station was originally located. Two nurses and two laborers will be assigned to work in shifts day and night to improve efficiency. The plan is to use the savings in medical treatment fees from the reduced number of patients sent to the Ji Liao Hospital to offset the regular expenses. The cost of adding the beds and equipment is estimated at 1,000 yuan, and the Bureau has instructed the General Affairs Office to approve it.

Weather Report 204

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the sky was cloudy, there were moderate northeastern winds in the East China Sea and the Taiwan Strait, and there were southerly to southwestern winds on the Shandong coast. The weather in the China Sea was bad due to a hurricane that may move towards the coast of Annam. The low pressure center northeast of Yap may move west-northwest. As of 6:00 AM this morning, the center of the hurricane was within 120 miles of 16 degrees north latitude and 114 degrees east longitude. The wind force was unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 70.9 degrees and the lowest was 44.6 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 71.2 degrees and the lowest was 55.4 degrees.

Education News

Important Resolutions of the Vocational Education Design Committee of the Ministry of Education in Other Provinces (Part 2) 206

(A) Investigation (1) Provinces and Cities (Directly-administered Municipalities) (1) Matters to be investigated by the educational administrative organs of the provinces and cities: (a) The number of public and private junior and senior middle schools within the jurisdiction (including the number of primary schools within the city limits, etc.); (b) The number of students in public and private junior and senior middle schools within the jurisdiction (including actual numbers and the ratio with junior high school graduates); (c) The employment situation of graduates from public and private junior and senior middle schools within the jurisdiction in the past three years (the number of students entering higher education, the number of employed, and the number of unemployed should include actual numbers and percentages, as well as the percentages of various industries within the employed); (d) The types, number of students, and employment situation of vocational schools at all levels within the jurisdiction (same as item (c)); (e) The maximum amount of educational funds in this province or city that can be allocated to vocational education, and other methods of raising special funds for vocational education; (2) Matters to be investigated by the construction administrative organs of the province and city, the municipal social bureau, or other relevant administrative organs: (a) The types and number of well-known factories and stores within the jurisdiction, the number of employees, wages, and the knowledge and skills required for service; (b) The main raw materials and their quantities within the jurisdiction, and the ability to develop certain industries in the shortest possible time; (c) The current situation of inherent key handicraft industries and semi-mechanized industries within the jurisdiction, and the approximate number of workers; (d) The most important agricultural products within the jurisdiction and their total output; (2) Counties and Cities: (1) Matters to be investigated by the educational administrative organs of the counties and cities: (a) The situation of primary school graduates within the jurisdiction, and their family occupations and economic conditions (same as (A)(1)(c)); (b) The family occupations and economic conditions of junior high school students within the jurisdiction; (c) The employment situation of graduates from vocational schools at all levels within the jurisdiction (same as item (a)); (d) The maximum amount of educational funds in this county or city that can be allocated to vocational education, and other methods of raising special funds for vocational education; (2) Matters to be investigated by the construction administrative organs of the counties and cities: (a) The types of factories and stores and the most important handicrafts within the jurisdiction, as well as the number of workers, approximate wages, production and sales quantities, etc.; (b) The agricultural situation within the jurisdiction; (c) Whether there are any public or private agricultural experiment stations or new-style improved farms, etc., within the jurisdiction that have achieved results or have a good environment for development. The above investigation methods are a complete plan in preparation for the establishment of vocational schools at all levels in various regions in the future. The time required will necessarily be slightly longer. If various regions urgently want to open schools, they can first determine the types (rural, industrial, or commercial) and then conduct investigations based on the relevant items listed above within the planned scope, which will be simpler and faster. At the same time, educational administrative organs at all levels and relevant organs must still conduct detailed investigations at any time to prepare for the continuous establishment of vocational schools. The following three points should be noted: (1) The number of graduates of a certain type that can be accommodated by the original various industries in the local area at present and in the near future; (2) What kind of industries are currently being planned and built at present and in the near future, and the number of vocational graduates of a certain type required; (3) The number of interns that can be accommodated by local industrial institutions at present and in the near future. After the establishment standards are set, the subjects, levels, curriculum, and study period of all vocational schools in a region should be comprehensively regulated and should not be easily changed within a one-year period.

(B) Establishment: After the investigation results are obtained, the following points should be noted regarding the environment, equipment, funding, teachers, and students before establishing a school: (1) Environment: (1) The location of agricultural vocational schools should be in rural areas in principle. If it is unavoidable, it can be located in the suburbs with a rural environment; (2) More than 60% of the students enrolled in agricultural vocational schools at the primary level should be children of farmers; (3) The location of industrial vocational schools should be: (a) Where there are handicrafts or semi-mechanized industries that can be developed and improved locally; (b) Where there are handicrafts or semi-mechanized industries that are gradually declining and should be urgently improved and remedied; (c) Where there are no such industries but there are abundant raw materials that can be used to promote manufacturing; (d) Where there are factories that can be used for internships; (4) When recruiting new students for industrial vocational schools, priority should be given to recruiting children of workers or those who are willing to engage in this profession; (5) Commercial vocational schools should be established in large urban commercial areas first. Other ordinary counties and cities should first establish agricultural and industrial disciplines; (6) When recruiting students for commercial vocational schools, priority should be given to recruiting children of merchants or those who are willing to engage in commerce; (7) Vocational schools at all levels and in all disciplines should negotiate cooperation methods with relevant local organizations and groups, such as students being recommended by them, internships being borrowed from their facilities, and trial employment after graduation, etc.; (2) Funding and Equipment: (1) The funding for vocational schools at all levels, except for special expenses, should not be lower than that of equivalent schools for ordinary recurring expenses; (2) When preparing the education budget, education administrative organs at all levels should specifically list an item for vocational education funding, and consider the situation in various regions, stipulate proportions, and increase the amount and percentage of the total education funding year by year; (3) Vocational schools at all levels should not charge tuition fees in principle, and should try to exempt or reduce the fees for internship materials, etc.; (4) Vocational schools at all levels should have the minimum regulations for internship sites and work equipment, which should be stipulated and announced by education administrative organs at all levels based on the actual situation. In agricultural disciplines, the area of cultivated land and the types and number of new agricultural tools should be specified. In industrial disciplines, the area of the factory and the types and number of machines should be specified. In primary technical disciplines (typing, barbering, auto repair, etc.), the types and number of practice equipment should be specified. If it is not possible to purchase all of them, special agreements can be made with stores for rental or borrowing methods; (5) All income from farms and factories operated by vocational schools at all levels should be included in the budget; (3) Teachers: (1) Vocational teachers at all levels must have vocational knowledge, skills, and experience. The regulations for their appointment will be formulated separately by the Ministry of Education; (2) Vocational teachers at all levels should operate together with students as a service principle; (3) The salaries of vocational teachers at all levels should not be lower than those of teachers at equivalent schools. Those with special knowledge, skills, and experience should be appropriately increased; (4) Measures for teacher training in vocational schools will be formulated separately; (4) Students' Prospects: (1) When establishing vocational schools, it is necessary to identify handicrafts or simple mechanical industries that can be developed locally and do not require a lot of capital, so that students can engage in independent occupations after graduation; (2) Vocational schools should cooperate with local vocational institutions to prepare for the establishment of a certain business to train its staff; (3) Vocational schools must establish a career placement department and liaise with vocational guidance centers in the vicinity; (4) Vocational schools should liaise with local vocational circles so that students can be asked to try out their skills after graduation; (5) Vocational schools should conduct detailed investigations into the service performance and status of graduates and provide guidance for improvement at any time.

Standards for Practical Training of Vocational School Students 207

1. Practical Training Locations: There are four types of practical training for vocational schools: (1) The school establishes its own farms, factories, stores, and so on for students to use for practical training; (2) The school designates a large farm for students to organize, manage, cultivate, and harvest as a practical training location; (3) The school liaises and cooperates with vocational institutions of the same nature, so that students spend part of their time attending classes at the school and part of their time doing practical training at various institutions; (4) A vocational school of the same nature is attached to an industrial institution, and students do practical training in the factory of the original institution. When running vocational schools, the above four items should be considered and adopted based on the actual local conditions.

2. Practical Training Time: (1) The total amount of practical training time for students in various vocational schools should account for more than half of the total number of class hours in principle; (2) The daily practical training time for students should not be separated and should be at least four consecutive hours in principle; (3) The arrangement of student coursework should be based on the principle of attending classes in the morning and doing practical training in the afternoon. If it is due to the relationship of the practical training location, practical training may also be done in the morning; (4) The distribution of student practical training in each academic year should be based on the principle of learning before studying. For example, in the first few years, there is more practical training time and less class time, while in the later academic years, there is less practical training time and more class time; (5) The practical training time for agricultural subjects such as rice cultivation and sericulture may be appropriately changed.

3. Practical Training Divisions: Agricultural practical training should designate areas, industrial practical training should designate objects, commercial practical training should designate items, and household practical training should designate items or objects. The organization of student practical training is roughly divided into the following three types: (1) Individual practical training, such as dividing areas for cultivation in agriculture and making individual pieces in industry; (2) Group practical training, such as several people jointly cultivating in agriculture and several people cooperating in industry; (3) Joint practical training, such as students of the same level or several levels jointly cultivating in agriculture and students of the same level or several levels cooperating in industry.

4. Key Points of Practical Training: (1) Various vocational schools should have concrete and detailed plans for the practical training outline; (2) Each type of practice should have a teaching plan that includes the purpose, method, materials, tools, work procedures, and performance evaluation; (3) The distribution of practical training materials should be based on basic practice first, followed by applied practice; (4) The planned program should be implemented in sequence to achieve the original purpose and the practical training process must be recorded; (5) You must concentrate and be dedicated during practical training, and be meticulous, and avoid being sloppy; (6) During practical training, you must be agile and not waste time; (7) Teachers and students should work together to indicate the path at any time; (8) Do not arbitrarily waste practical training materials for various vocational schools, or seeds for agricultural matters, etc., and take into account the principles of production and economy; (9) In addition to caring for and organizing public utensils after practical training or practical training, pay attention to repairs at any time; (10) The products must be of excellent quality and must have commercial value for comparison and assessment; (11) Commercial practical training should be precise and quick and the most important point is to treat customers kindly and amiably; (12) The rules of practical training must be strictly observed; (13) Labor work should take into account the health and physical strength of students; (14) If the products are sold, if there is a surplus in addition to the cost, a percentage should be awarded to the students; (15) When there is a need for people during busy farming seasons or in factories, students may be asked to help in order to gain practical training, and the wages may be used by the student who assisted in the work.

Outline of the Number of Class Hours for Various Disciplines in Vocational Schools Promulgated by the Ministry of Education (6) 208

(1) Bank Bookkeeping Department: (1) Purpose: To train intermediate staff in bank bookkeeping; (2) Age of Admission: 15-22; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 2 hours, Arithmetic 2 hours, English 4 hours, Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Bank Bookkeeping Subjects) 16 hours, (Bank Bookkeeping Practice) 20 hours, totaling 45 hours.

(C) Regarding Business

(1) Bank Bookkeeping Department: (1) Purpose: To train intermediate staff in bank bookkeeping; (2) Age of Admission: 15-22; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 2 hours, Arithmetic 2 hours, English 4 hours, Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Bank Bookkeeping Subjects) 16 hours, (Bank Bookkeeping Practice) 20 hours, totaling 45 hours.

(2) Accounting Department: (1) Purpose: To train intermediate accountants; (2) Age of Admission: 15-22; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 2 hours, Arithmetic 3 hours, English 4 hours, Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Accounting Subjects) 16 hours, (Accounting Practice) 20 hours, totaling 46 hours.

(3) Insurance Department: (1) Purpose: To train intermediate staff in the insurance industry; (2) Age of Admission: 15-22; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 2 hours, Arithmetic 3 hours, English 4 hours, Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Insurance Subjects) 18 hours, (Insurance Industry Practice) 18 hours, totaling 46 hours.

(4) Remittance Department: (1) Purpose: To train intermediate staff in the remittance industry; (2) Age of Admission: 15-22; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 2 hours, Arithmetic 3 hours, English 4 hours, Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Remittance Subjects) 16 hours, (Remittance Industry Practice) 20 hours, totaling 46 hours.

(5) Secretarial Department: (1) Purpose: To train secretarial personnel in shorthand, typing, and document processing; (2) Age of Admission: 18-25; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 4 hours, English 4 hours, Calligraphy 2 hours, Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Shorthand Typing and Secretarial Subjects) 12 hours, (Shorthand Typing and Secretarial Practice) 24 hours, totaling 47 hours.

(6) Commercial Advertising Department: (1) Purpose: To train commercial advertising design and drawing personnel; (2) Age of Admission: 15-22; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 2 hours, English 3 hours, Drawing 4 hours, Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Advertising Subjects) 16 hours, (Advertising Practice) 20 hours, totaling 46 hours.

(7) Transportation Department: (1) Purpose: To train intermediate staff in the transportation industry; (2) Age of Admission: 18-22; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 2 hours, English 4 hours, Arithmetic 2 hours, Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Transportation Subjects) 18 hours, (Transportation Practice) 18 hours, totaling 45 hours.

(D) Regarding Home Economics

(1) Sewing Department: (1) Purpose: To train technicians in improving and operating the sewing industry; (2) Age of Admission: 15-22; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 2 hours (limited to female students), Home Economics 2 hours, Drawing Hours, Music 1 hour (limited to female students), Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Sewing Work Methods) 10 hours, (Sewing Practice) 26 hours, totaling 44 hours or 41 hours.

(2) Embroidery Department: (1) Purpose: To train embroidery technicians; (2) Age of Admission: 15-22; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 2 hours, Calligraphy 2 hours, Music 1 hour (limited to female students), Drawing 3 hours, Home Economics 2 hours (limited to female students), Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Embroidery Work Methods) 8 hours, (Embroidery Practice) 26 hours, totaling 45 hours or 42 hours.

(3) Nursing Department: (1) Purpose: To train nursing talents for hospitals and clinics; (2) Age of Admission: 15-25; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 2 hours, Physiology and Hygiene 2 hours, Psychology 1 hour, English 2 hours, Music 1 hour (limited to female students) Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Nursing Subjects) 20 hours, (Nursing Practice) 18 hours, totaling 47 hours or 46 hours.

(4) Midwifery Department: (1) Purpose: To train midwifery talents for hospitals and general midwifery; (2) Age of Admission: 18-25; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 2 hours, Physiology and Hygiene 2 hours, Music 1 hour, English 2 hours, Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Midwifery Subjects) 20 hours, (Midwifery Practice) 18 hours, totaling 46 hours.

(5) General Home Economics Department: (1) Purpose: To train excellent housewives; (2) Age of Admission: 15-22; (3) Length of Study: Three years; (4) Subjects: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 3 hours, Physiology and Hygiene 2 hours, Music 1 hour, Drawing 1 hour, Physics and Chemistry 2 hours, Physical Education 20 minutes daily; (Home Economics Subjects) 14 hours, (Home Economics Practice) 20 hours, totaling 44 hours.

(3) Senior Vocational Schools (Recruiting Primary School Graduates) 210

Senior vocational schools recruit primary school graduates and those with equivalent academic qualifications. The length of study is five years. The teaching subjects and class hours for the first two academic years of various vocational schools are tentatively set as follows: (General Subjects) Civics 1 hour, Chinese 4 hours, Arithmetic 3 hours, History 2 hours, Geography 2 hours, Physics and Chemistry 2 hours, Biology 2 hours, Drawing 1 hour, English 3 hours, Physical Education 2 hours; (Vocational Subjects) 4 hours, (Vocational Practice) 18 hours, totaling 44 hours. The teaching subjects and class hours for the third, fourth, and fifth academic years should be in accordance with the regulations for senior vocational schools recruiting junior high school graduates in Section 2. However, the teaching hours for general subjects may be appropriately increased, but the teaching hours for vocational subjects must not be reduced by more than one-fifth.

General Instructions 211

(1) Subjects closely related to vocational knowledge and skills, such as applied mechanics in the mechanical engineering department, chemical experiments in the applied chemistry department, calligraphy and patterns in the embroidery department, and commercial geography in the business department, as well as social surveys in the rural cooperation department, may also be included in the scope of vocational subjects.

(2) Subjects such as experiments, design, and drafting in vocational subjects shall be included in the scope of vocational practice according to their nature.

(3) Vocational subjects should include subjects on the enterprise, operation, management, and all practical economics of the profession being studied.

(4) Physical education for all subjects in the first and second types of vocational schools shall adopt a daily exercise break system, held in the middle of the practice work time according to the scheduled hours.

(5) The prescribed hours for each general subject are not completely evenly distributed among the semesters, and should be freely and actively allocated in each semester according to the actual needs of learning.

(6) The total number of vocational subjects and practice hours is the average number for each academic year, and should be freely and actively allocated in each semester according to the actual situation.

(7) The selection of general subject teaching materials must be based on those related to the profession being studied. For example, civics, in addition to paying attention to general civic common sense, should pay attention to the service ethics of various vocational departments; Chinese and English should pay attention to the special applied texts of various industries; and mathematics should pay attention to practical applications such as bookkeeping and abacus. (End)

Ministry of Education Interprets Educational Laws and School System 212

The Ministry of Education has issued three interpretations regarding educational laws and school systems, which are excerpted below:

(1) Regarding the matter of private schools not being allowed to add branch campuses, the order to the Jiangsu Education Department stated briefly that private schools may not branch out. If the number of students is large and one location cannot accommodate them, the school buildings may be divided into two locations, but they must still be within the same local area.

(2) Regarding the Shanghai Education Bureau's request for instructions on whether other secondary schools besides those affiliated with the model school can set up attached primary schools, the order to the bureau stated that private secondary schools, if needed in reality, can also set up primary schools and kindergartens. However, these original primary schools and kindergartens should be handled in accordance with the regulations for private schools and adopt a specific name, and should not continue to be called affiliated primary schools or affiliated kindergartens.

(3) Regarding whether the property of the Education Association should be kept in the custody of the guiding agency or the supervising agency after the Education Association is disbanded, the order to the Fujian Education Department stated that the provincial party headquarters, special municipal party headquarters, and county and city party headquarters guide the Education Association and reorganize and organize methods, etc., which refer to the old Education Association. If the county Education Association is an Education Association organized in accordance with the law, its property after dissolution should be kept in the custody of the liquidator, who has the power to represent the Education Association in carrying out all liquidation matters, in accordance with the provisions of Article 36 of the Education Association Law.

Wang Qi and Others Petition the Ministry of Education to Revise the Sino-German Art Exhibition Method 215

(Central Telegram, Nanjing, 26th) The Ministry of Education's preparations for the Sino-German Art Exhibition have been underway for a long time. The host, Liu Haisu, is scheduled to go to Germany on November 14 to open the exhibition. Wang Qi and others believe that the association did not publicly solicit works or publicly exhibit and review them in the country beforehand, and it is said that Liu is carrying elephant films, which they deeply fear will affect the honor of the national culture. Therefore, they have jointly petitioned the Ministry of Education to revise the public exhibition review method and order Da Haisu to postpone his trip to Germany in order to be cautious and avoid a decline in international cultural status. Wang and others have also sent representatives to the Ministry of Education, where they were received by Duan Xipeng, who promised to forward the matter to Minister Wang for review.

County Education Bureau Issues a Notice to Pay Attention to Imprints 220

The Shanghai County Education Bureau recently issued an instruction to all levels of schools, social education agencies, and kindergartens stating: "According to the instruction from the Jiangsu Provincial Education Department, it has been found that various county bureaus have reported the loss of imprints by county primary schools due to various reasons, requesting supplementary issuance for application, etc. In addition to separate instructions to comply, it is found that school imprints are to demonstrate credibility and should be carefully preserved. Now, losses occur from time to time, indicating that the principals of various primary schools do not know the importance of and neglect the management of the school. In addition to separate orders, the director of the bureau is hereby specially instructed to instruct the principals of various primary schools that if the loss of imprints occurs again in the future, the principal should be immediately dismissed to show punishment. I hope you will all bear this in mind and not forget. This order, etc., is hereby notified for your attention and careful safekeeping. This order."

Recent Work of the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association; Preparing to Establish Ordinary and Laboring Childcare Centers; Drafting All Methods for the Children's Year 225

On the Children's Day commemorative day of April 4 this year, the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, Health Bureau, Social Bureau, and Public Security Bureau jointly held a celebration. It was felt that the development of children's causes could not be achieved by holding a commemorative event on Children's Day. There must be a permanent organization to gradually seek the welfare of children. Therefore, the four bureaus of education, health, social affairs, and public security were jointly responsible for preparing and organizing the Shanghai Children's Welfare Committee, drafting simple rules, and submitting them to the municipal government for record in mid-May. In mid-June, in view of the difficulties faced by laborers in factories in raising children, the Committee also launched the organization of the Childcare Business Committee to prepare for childcare centers. By mid-August, in accordance with the regulations, enthusiastic children's organizations and experts were hired to serve as committee members, and the committee was formally established. It has been two months since then, and efforts have been made to carry out various causes. The recent work of the association is recorded as follows:

Internal Organization: The association has one president, one chairman of the standing committee, six standing committee members, and one secretary. It also has five departments: the Children's Protection Department, the Children's Health Department, the Children's Research Department, and the Children's Business Department. Each department has one director and several committee members.

Responsible Personnel: President Wu Tiecheng, Chairman of the Standing Committee Pan Gongzhan, Standing Committee Members Li Tingan, Chen Heqin, Hu Shuyi, Wang Guanyi, Liu Wang Liming, Zhao Zengqi, Director of the Children's Protection Department, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Director of the Children's Health Department, Director of the Municipal Health Bureau, Director of the Children's Research Department Chen Heqin, Director of the Children's Business Department, the China Child Welfare Association, Secretary Zhou Wanghe.

General Affairs: The association's business includes the Children's Protection Department, which specializes in protecting children's lives and rights, prohibiting abuse, inheritance, and all rescue matters; the Children's Health Department, which handles children's health and nutrition matters; the Children's Research Department, which handles design, children's psychological testing, and all investigation and statistics matters; the Children's Business Department, which organizes businesses such as childcare centers and educational institutions.

Preparing to Build a Clubhouse: The association is a permanent organization in Shanghai for the welfare of children. It plans to raise donations to build its own clubhouse. Currently, it is temporarily borrowing the Municipal Education Bureau on Daji Road in West Gate as its address. The mailing address is 205 Shandong Road.

Recent Work: The recent work of the association is as follows: (1) Preparing to establish two ordinary childcare centers and one laboring childcare center; (2) Drafting all methods for the Children's Year next year and submitting them to the National Government for record; (3) Designing and carrying out various children's causes in the city.

Recent News from Shen Bao Correspondence School of Journalism; A Glimpse of the Course Content; Continuing to Recruit New Students 227

The third batch of new students recruited by the Shen Bao Correspondence School of Journalism last time has started classes on the 18th of this month. This time, the new students recruited for the third batch after the examination have also started classes at the same time. The lecture notes for the old students of the first and second batches have also been continuously issued. This time, a total of sixteen kinds of lecture notes have been issued, namely: 1. Chinese Language, 2. Practical Journalism, 3. Newspaper Printing Technology, 4. Newspaper Management and Organization, 5. Advertising, 6. Research on Current Affairs Issues, 7. Publishing Law, 8. Journalist Common Sense, 9. Introduction to Journalism, 10. Foreign Journalism, 11. Prose Research, 12. Newspaper Distribution, 13. Correspondence Practice, 14. Commentary Writing, 15. Selected Readings of English Newspapers, 16. Domestic Journalism. The school has decided to issue lecture notes four times a month in the future, and it is stated that if no accidents occur, they can be issued on schedule each time without delay. Each lecture note is accompanied by exercises, and students are very interested in studying them. All kinds of lecture notes have been carefully compiled by the professors and have not been published to the outside world. The content is rich and the explanation is detailed, so it is very valuable. It is not only available for current study, but also available for permanent reference. Monthly exams will also be held on schedule. All of this is good news for those who have entered the school and is worth praising for the school. Secondly, in addition to the students who have been admitted for the third batch of new students this time and have started classes at the same time as the students who were previously recruited for the third batch, there are also students who have registered but have not submitted their test papers to the school. In addition, the school has received quite a few people who have gone to ask for the articles of association these days. In order to avoid missing the opportunity, the deadline for recruiting the third batch of students has been postponed, and the number of students has been expanded to continue recruiting so that those who arrive later can continue to join.

National Martial Arts Examination Extended for Three Days and Ends; Hunan and Fujian Athletes Misunderstand Yesterday; After Persuasion, They Have Agreed to Play 238

(Nanjing, 26th) On the 26th, the seventh day of the National Health Examination, it was originally scheduled to end on the 27th, but because the various competitions could not be finished, it was extended for another three days. The re-examinations of various competitions have been completed, and the semi-finals and finals will be held afterwards. There were few spectators on the 26th morning, but there were many in the afternoon. A dispute occurred at the venue in the afternoon. During the boxing match between Hunan and Fujian, the Fujian athlete hit the Hunan athlete in the eye. According to the examination rules, the eye is a vital part, and touching it is considered a foul. The Hunan athlete then appealed to the referees, who forbade him to speak and ordered him to continue the competition. The Hunan athlete also punched the Fujian athlete in the face, and the Fujian athlete bled on the spot.

The referee immediately recognized that the Hunan athlete had fouled and revoked his qualification. A referee from Hunan then came out to interfere, and the two referees argued and twisted out of the examination venue. All the athletes from Hunan also withdrew from the venue in formation to show their overall forfeiture. According to Zhang Zhijiang, today's dispute was a misunderstanding between the two athletes. If they could have obeyed the referee's orders at that time, there would have been no dispute. After the Hunan team leader persuaded the Hunan athletes, they have calmed down and have agreed to take the examination.

Xu Chengji Left Shanghai Yesterday, Will Return Next April 239

Messrs. Xu Chengji and Lin Xuyin, the overseas Chinese tennis players from the Dutch East Indies Java for the National Games, returned to Shanghai from Beijing a few days ago. Also on board were Mr. and Mrs. Ruan Kunli, newly appointed assistant at the Chinese Consulate in Penang, British Malaya, by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.
