Spring and Autumn

Legend is the Enemy of Progress 246

— Pei Yu

Near the greatest and most beautiful Niagara Falls in America, there is a power plant. On the wall of a generator room in the plant, there is an eye-catching and touching announcement. The announcement reads: "Legend is the enemy of progress."

If I were a young man, I would definitely copy the words on this announcement and hang them in my own study as a motto. Why? Because these few words answer a question that many ambitious young people often think about and often say: "What kind of opportunity can enable me to make a great and earth-shattering career in society and in the world? What is that opportunity?"

Even if there is a sound that exceeds the thunderous sound of that large power plant, the eight words on the announcement always clearly guarantee that various opportunities are waiting for you. Because the mere eight words contain an absolute guarantee that opportunities have never knocked on the doors of young people more loudly than they do now.

You may say: "What you said is certainly very reasonable. I wonder if you can provide some facts to prove it?"

Yes; I think I can.

First, the hub of our country's industry and commerce is now in the hands of a group of young leaders. We can almost see in newspapers and magazines every day that young people have become bank presidents, company managers, factory technicians, and so on. In other words, young people have become the driving force for progress. When I say the word "young people," I am not limited to people in leadership positions who are 20, 30, or some other clearly defined age. I use these two words in a broad sense.

What I mean is that they have novel ideas, far-sighted vision, solid skills, broad knowledge, firm perseverance, courageous spirit, diligent spirit, sound physique, pleasant state of mind, and they relentlessly and painstakingly explore the treasures before them. That is the true meaning of the two words "young people." This continuous and eager aspiration of young people, this indomitable perseverance, is indeed the driving force for the development of our country's current industry and commerce, and it is also a strong backing for the progress of all undertakings. If you do not believe the saying "Legend is the enemy of progress," and blindly stick to conventions, or superstitiously believe in fate, or hesitate and doubt, or shrink back, then you will never succeed and will greatly fail the opportunities at your door.

Fame and Fortune 247

— Qifenglou Master

During the Qianlong era of the Qing Dynasty, there was abundant harvest and prosperity, and the world was at peace. Therefore, Emperor Gaozong (Qianlong), in a very leisurely mood, left the palace on a southern tour, traveling around the famous scenic spots of Jiangnan. One day, accompanied by a high monk, he went to the seaside to look out, only to see sails coming and going in the sea like weaving. Emperor Gaozong asked the monk, "How many ships are there in the sea?" The monk replied, "There are only two." Emperor Gaozong wondered, "How do you know?" The monk replied, "One is for 'fame' and the other is for 'fortune,' that's all." According to the current ships in the sea, I am afraid that in the near future, it will be reduced to only one, because people are all pursuing profit, and how many people are still asking for fame!

Some people say, "Fame" is virtual, and "fortune" is real. In fact, this statement is specious. You must know that "fame" and "fortune" are related, and seeking fortune with fame is the right way. Gaining profit by fraud and trickery is not only improper, but can only gain temporary benefits and will never last long. However, people nowadays only know how to pursue the present, and who cares about future failures.

As for gaining both fame and fortune, who does not hope for it? But before becoming famous, one should not have thoughts of profit in mind. One should always be conscientious and work hard, only moving forward on the right path to fame! To achieve knowing what others do not know, being able to do what others cannot do, and not caring about hardships and dangers. If so, I know that there will be a day of fame. When you have gained a good reputation, of course, people from all sides will come to seek you. At that time, you will not need to spend any more effort, and naturally fortune will come with fame.

Rural Sketches 248

— Xiang

(1) Picking Cotton

One by one, carrying bamboo baskets on their backs, old, young, male, female, some wearing straw hats, some with blue cloth wrapped around their heads...

In the morning, they run out of the village five li away, running alone, running in groups...

Running east, west, south, and north to all their cotton fields.

White, soft, clusters of cotton, soft and white cotton, they all bow their heads, carefully harvesting, and putting it into the basket on their backs. Clusters of soft and white cotton, already heated through, falling on the sand, they also bow their heads, gently pick it up, and put it into the basket on their backs in the same way.

From morning to night, from today to tomorrow, until all the cotton is picked, you can only see them carrying the empty baskets out and carrying them back full of cotton.

Although their bodies are very painful, their spirits may be very comforted. Their hearts are as pure as the cotton.

(2) Reaping Rice

The setting sun dyes the fields golden, and the dying autumn cicadas still chirp "zhiliao, zhiliao," chirping very sadly.

An elderly farmer happily carries the ripe rice on his shoulders from their field to the yard at home, showing his final victory.

Several young farmers hold sickles and keep cutting their rice, without resting for a moment.

Cutting, carrying, gradually turning the golden fields into ocher-black soil.

From sowing, transplanting seedlings, drawing water,... peacefully obtaining today's harvest, hoping for this year, hoping for next year,... as long as there are no natural disasters or man-made disasters,... their hard work will not be in vain.

(3) Threshing Rice

"Pata,... pata,"

A young couple sings a rural love song, and their hands beat the rice on the threshing floor against each other, making such a sound, as if clapping to their beat.

"Suoluo,... suoluo," this is the sound of the grain falling down.

Singing, threshing, and the sound of falling grain, a wonderful trio, is playing in this great nature.

The songs are sung continuously, the rice is threshed continuously,... they do not feel hard or tired, they are already intoxicated.

Roosters, hens, in groups of three or five, regardless of the owner's year-long expectations and hard work, secretly eat the grain on all sides, and their owner does not even notice, perhaps unwilling to disturb them.

Willing to let the chickens eat some of the grain exchanged for sweat, they are truly intoxicated.

Singing, threshing, and the sound of falling grain, this wonderful trio, is still playing in great nature.

Modern Opening 249

— Mei Xue

The opening piece is popular again for a while now, and it can often be seen in newspapers and radio broadcasts. However, very few of them are in the tone of the opening piece. The opening piece is a special work in Suzhou literature, and people from other provinces and counties cannot write it. When they do, it always has some awkward and strange tones. Poets will also not write it, because when they do, it tends to be more lyrical. Those who are not familiar with tones will not write it, because when they do, it is close to a beachy tone. Because of these three inabilities, good poems are often seen, but good opening pieces are extremely rare. Recently, in a certain book hall, I heard a modern opening piece that was quite amusing, and the tones were harmonious, the rhythm was appropriate, and the writing was between elegant and vulgar. It was indeed an outstanding and appropriate good opening piece. It is said that it was written by a certain gentleman, and this gentleman is a famous expert in opening pieces. Of course, he has works that meet the standards. It is a pity that my memory is weak, and I only remember the beginning part. It is written below: The golden wind and jade dew intersect in autumn, and the insects chirp sadly without stopping. It is not only the autumn insects that feel resentment, but even the modern girls also add to their sorrows. May I ask, what is causing the girls to feel sorrow and depression? They are not worried about food or clothing, but only hate that the autumn coolness makes it difficult to show off. Georgette and Indian silk are now useless and must be placed on the top floor; they can only reveal a touching affection, failing to show off the two fleshy buns on their chests... When singing to this point, the whole hall burst into laughter.

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 250

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 17: Who Can Be Without Emotion? Home Thoughts Discourage Soldiers; Warfare Does Not Dislike Deception; Bold Words Strengthen Military Hearts

When Zhao Ziqiang saw them pushing the squad leader to ask for help, he couldn't refuse. He had to take out the money and give it to the squad leader to handle. The thirty yuan departure fee from the regimental headquarters was collected by the quartermaster at six o'clock yesterday afternoon. Until now, Zhao Ziqiang had not put the money in his pocket and kept it. When he roughly counted it, he had already spent a lot of it. Although Zhao Ziqiang felt very aggrieved, he couldn't say anything. With great difficulty, he got through this period, and the regimental headquarters had already called, urging him to collect the luggage carts. According to the rules, each company needs six carts, two small luggage carts for ammunition and four large luggage carts for office supplies, cooking utensils, and tents. However, this time, only four carts were called for collection. The regimental headquarters specified that these four carts should all carry large luggage. Two more carts for small luggage were still needed, and each battalion had to find a way to get them. It seems that it is not too difficult for the First Battalion and Fourth Company to find eight carts. However, the peasants near the barracks did not dare to prepare carts. Moreover, the news that the army was about to set off had already spread, and people with livestock quickly hid them. At this time, the First Battalion was short eight carts, each battalion was short eight carts, and the whole division was short more than a hundred carts. With only a few hours left, where could they find a way? Zhao Ziqiang ran back and forth between the company headquarters and the battalion headquarters for this problem. Their battalion commander, Bao Fang, was indeed an experienced officer, so he asked him: "Now that things have come to this, it's not a matter of grabbing at straws. Your home is in Haidian. If you go there yourself, you can definitely get two carts. If that doesn't work, you'll have to make do, find a few pack animals, find a few civilians. If you have to use compulsory measures, you'll have to use a little. Anyway, we'll return the livestock and civilians to them in the future, and our conscience will be clear." Zhao Ziqiang was sweating profusely, and he had not even thought of returning to Haidian. (224)

Miscellaneous Notes on the Post National Games 251

— Yin Qiu

—After the Second Performance of the 10,000-Meter Race—

In this grand National Games, the problem of Jin Zhongkang running one lap less in the 10,000-meter race unexpectedly occurred, which caused a lot of disputes. It cannot be said that it was not an unfortunate event for the Games! Although it was decided at that time to cancel Jin Zhongkang's first place, this problem still felt suspicious? Some people said, "The ranking of the 10,000-meter race is like arbitrarily pairing mandarin ducks"; others said, "The score of the 10,000-meter race is a muddled account." People who care about sports are all discussing it there.

Since the performance race of the 10,000 meters on the afternoon of the 19th, Jin Zhongkang eventually won the first place, but the result was slightly worse, and the time was two minutes slower than the last time; so, I heard a lot of comments again.

Some people said, "Jin Zhongkang's skills are extraordinary after all. He definitely did not run one lap less the first time. If he really ran one lap less, and his ability was to be after tenth place, how could he be so presumptuous? Boldly take the risk of re-performing? If he really lags behind one lap and is not as good as others, wouldn't he expose his ugliness and prove that he did run less, leaving endless shame? Jin Zhongkang would not be so foolish."

Another person said, "Jin Zhongkang's flaw is that the results of the two races differed by two minutes, failing to completely clear people's suspicion about running one lap less. This needs to be explained."

The former person said again, "There are several reasons for the difference of two minutes: First, the wind was strong that day, and it was very difficult to run to the East Commander's Platform, so everyone's results were poor. Second, everyone's results were not particularly outstanding, so Jin took maintaining the first place as the limit. Since no one competed fiercely with him, Jin had no opportunity to make rapid progress. Third, running two 10,000-meter races in the middle of just a few days requires a lot of strength. Now that the five athletes ran 20,000 meters each, the results should naturally be worse. Fourth, and further thinking, Jin Zhongkang may have caused people to suspect him because of his excellent results last time, so there was a saying that he ran one lap less; so this time, he deliberately relaxed, slowed down two minutes, and leisurely showed that he was still enough to overwhelm the others. Then, it is undoubtedly true that he accelerated in the initial race, quickly occupying the first place by two minutes!"

That person also said, "What you said is true, but thinking it over, Jin Zhongkang may have run one lap less in the initial race, and fortunately won the second performance, which was to save his reputation, so how could he not work hard? Therefore, it was easy to win; under hard work, although he won the first place, the result was still worse, isn't it still because of one lap?"

The former person explained again, "Jin Zhongkang's problem of running less started with the accusation of the Shanxi team after the official announcement of the first place; then, wouldn't the athletes of the Shanxi team, Gu Desheng and Wang Zhenglin, etc., also work together to maintain the previous record, or even exceed it, so that Jin Zhongkang could not win the championship? Then Jin's victory is not easy! And among the five participants, any one of the other four got the first place, and Jin was second, which shows how difficult it will be for Jin to win the first place? As a result, Jin won it, and Jin's strength can be known, so it can be proved that Jin's victory last time was accurate, and running less is a suspicion."

Each member is willing to participate in this kind of performance race, which is a representation of sportsmanship and is worthy of our admiration! It further proves that the responsibility for the 10,000-meter dispute does not lie with the athletes participating in the race, but should be borne by the referee committee; the confusion of the referee committee led to this unfortunate event. Fortunately, there are these athletes with great understanding of justice who performed a second time, and it should be called a gentleman's competition.

There is another layer. When it was decided to cancel Jin Zhongkang's first place, it was based on Li Wenchang's record of 19 laps. So, Huang Bobin was greatly blamed, and his depression can be known. His resentment and frustration were no less than Jin's cancellation of the victory. It was not until after the second performance that Jin's satisfaction could be known, and Huang could also relieve some of his depression!

Overview of Global American Cotton Supply and Demand in the Last Quarter 266

– Consumption Is Higher Than Initially Expected –

According to a report from the New York Cotton Exchange News Agency, the world's cotton mills consumed more American cotton in the last quarter than initially estimated, about 273,000 bales more, that is, from 14,132,000 bales to 14,405,000 bales. The world's stock of American cotton at the end of July was 239,000 bales less than previously estimated, that is, from 11,975,000 bales to 11,705,000 bales. The reduction of 239,000 bales in the carryover offsets the increase of 980 bales in the government cotton production estimate, resulting in a decrease of 141,000 bales in the world's supply of American cotton this quarter. Therefore, the current supply is 24,066,000 bales, not 24,207,000 bales as previously estimated. The world's consumption of American cotton in the last quarter was 14,405,000 bales, the highest of any cotton season since 1928. In 1928-29, the world consumed 15,226,000 bales of American cotton. The carryover of 11,736,000 bales is above the recent average, but it is 1,452,000 bales less than last year. Last year's carryover was 12,228,000 bales.

Free Talk

Prophecy 276

— Zhi Shui

There is an English detective novelist named Conan Doyle, whose works were translated a lot by Lin Qinnan in the past. Western literary critics praised Mr. Ke's detective novels for being able to use the "achievements" of modern science, so although they are bizarre, they do not fall into absurdity.

So, this Mr. Ke is not an amateur in science. However, after the European War, we heard that this gentleman talked a lot about "Spiritualism," established societies, published periodicals, and gave lectures everywhere. Some people regarded the communication between humans and ghosts and the future of mankind as absurd, while others believed it to be revelation and prophecy.

There is also an English science fiction writer named Wells, whose international reputation is even greater. His "Outline of History" has also been translated into Chinese. Looking at his works, he can indeed be said to be a true scientist. However, a Reuters dispatch a few days ago said that he also made predictions about international politics in the past five years.

We believe that future changes in international politics can be predicted, but they must be based on the iron laws of social science, and then it is not a blind guess. Although Mr. Wells's "predictions" are much more beautiful than our "piling back maps," we always feel that they have a bit of Jianghu air. For example, he said that in the future, there will be a naval battle between Japan and the United States in the Pacific. The Japanese army will win first, but will be defeated by a plague, and then a great revolution will occur in Japan, etc., placing the factors of the great revolution on an unknowable plague.

Recently, newspapers have frequently reported that "the situation between Japan and Russia is dangerous," and political observers have said that 1935 will be a difficult year. People are panicking and turning to "prophecy." At this moment, a magazine issued a call for papers for the New Year's issue next year, with the topic of "The Future of Shanghai," which is to ask people to write some "predictions." The magazine editor's sense is the most sensitive, and they know that the vast readers are asking for "predictions." Originally, in this awkward situation, many people are extremely confused, and giving some reasonable "predictions" is a good thing and necessary.

However, if a "prediction" is reasonable, it will expose the Western mirror of some people. So we might as well "predict" first:

Truly reasonable predictions will not exist within China.

What is "Direction"? 277

— Gu Xiongfei

The film "Spring Silkworms" has been released, and some people criticize it as "sparse human direction."

"Sparse human direction," what does this mean? After thinking about it carefully, I reluctantly found an explanation: Western movie advertisements often say that there are thousands or tens of thousands of actors, while "Spring Silkworms" has only twenty or thirty people at most. Perhaps it means that there are too few people on stage. If there are too few, just say there are too few. Why say "sparse"? If the opposite of "sparse" is "dense," then hiring more extras and having them squeeze together tightly and filming it would be a film with a "climax"!

I am not a "film critic," so of course I don't want to discuss whether it is good or bad for people in the film to be "sparse" or "dense." What I want to say now is the meaning of the word "direction." Life is becoming more and more complex and changing. The original words are not enough, and more must be added. These new words can be newly created or imported, but they must have a clear meaning. But now we have to read articles embedded with many inexplicable new (?) words. The author seems to think that as long as he embeds some new words, his article will be valuable. "Direction" is one of them. It is used in articles and in conversations, but its meaning is ignored. It is really "depressing" to read and hear.

Originally, this is also a Japanese word, a stage play term.

Of course, a play must have a script, but having a script does not mean that there is a play to watch. There is also an important thing: how to materialize this script on the stage. This is called "direction" in Japanese, and we call it "rehearsal." Analyzing the theme and plot of the script, assigning roles, and unifying the stage equipment, scenery, and everything else that constitutes the play to make the script appear three-dimensionally on the stage丨this whole process is called "rehearsal." The person who undertakes this work is called the "director," and in Japanese it is called the "director." As for after the rehearsal is successful, when it is publicly performed on the stage for the audience, the "director" no longer cares about the control of the stage. That is the responsibility of the "stage supervisor."

An ideal "director" uses the background and props as his materials, not to mention that the actors are also his materials, and even the script is his material. He uses these to "create"; a good director has his unique "rehearsal method." Therefore, the same script can be rehearsed into very different things under the direction of different directors, and a bad director can make a mess of the script.

The recently performed "Roar, China" was successful in many ways, and its public release should receive the same attention from cultural circles as "Spring Silkworms." However, the impression I got this time was very different from the impression I got when I saw the Tsukiji Troupe perform the same script in Japan. To give the most common example: similarly, it is the awakening and resistance of the masses, but what the Drama Association rehearsed was a chaotic scene of just shouting slogans, while the scene rehearsed by the Tsukiji Troupe was full of the collective dynamic melody, which had actually broken through the scope of narrow "realism," and what filled the entire scene was not only "excitement," but a well-organized torrent of "power." This, needless to say, is a reflection of the different rehearsal methods of the directors, and also a reflection of the different degrees of worldview between the two directors and the different nature of the two groups, the Drama Association and the Tsukiji Troupe.

As for movies, the word "direction" cannot be used at all. Because, in movies, acting is not considered art. It is only considered art when it is captured by the camera from a certain angle and then replayed. Moreover, it cannot be replayed after it is captured. It must also be cut and arranged, and reorganized. There is a special term for this in film production, which cannot be confused with the "direction" of stage plays.

Literary Men Despise Each Other 278

— Yu Shixia

Zhao Yi's "Clumsy Examination of Everything" has an article about literary men despising each other, which describes the stories of literary men despising each other between the Qin and Han Dynasties and the Six Dynasties, which is already very detailed. In my opinion, literary men despising each other originated from the philosophers of the Zhou and Qin Dynasties. Confucius said, "People with different paths do not conspire with each other." The philosophers each held a theory and slandered each other. This is the ideological bias of those who despise each other. There is a saying today: "Those in the same industry are prone to jealousy." To slander others in order to praise oneself, and to express oneself in order to belittle others, this is the constant feeling in the psychology of those who despise each other. There is also a saying: "Three sentences cannot be separated from one's profession." Talking about the joys and sorrows of one's own work, and also discussing the gains and losses of colleagues, this is also the habit of those who despise each other in their language. Du Fu said, "Do not despise modern people and love ancient people." To express the nostalgic feelings of thinking about the past, and to sigh that those who come later are not as good as the ancients, this is the fallacy in the historical view of those who despise each other. What the ancients called liking cinnabar and disliking plain, discussing sweetness and avoiding bitterness, respecting the ancient and despising the present, valuing the distant and belittling the near, as well as favoring the same and attacking the different, and treating as master and slave, all seem to not go beyond these four points. Understanding this is to understand why literary men despise each other.

Since the Tang Dynasty, the stories of literary men despising each other are countless. Now, I will only briefly cite the example of fathers and sons who were both literary men and despised each other, to show that even as close as father and son, they do not give way to each other. Confucius only said that one should not give way to one's teacher when it comes to benevolence. Unexpectedly, there is actually a matter of not giving way to one's father when it comes to literature. During the Tang Dynasty, Lu Yuqing once transferred from Minister of the Right of the Ministry of Rites to Magistrate of Luochuan. When discussing matters, he was arrogant and unashamed, but when judging matters, his writing was nowhere to be found. Someone ridiculed him and said, "When speaking, his beak is three inches long, and when judging matters, his hand weighs five catties." His son also ridiculed him and said, "Lu Yuqing, his pen is weak and his mouth is hard. Once he receives a lawsuit, he cannot judge it in ten days." He sent the case under the bedding. Yuqing got it and read it, and said, "It must be that dog!" So he whipped him. During the Chenghua and Hongzhi periods of the Ming Dynasty, Li Dongyang's articles and titles were the highest in the world. One son, named Zhaoxian, with the courtesy name of Zhenbo, had the talent of reading several lines at a glance, and was known as surpassing his father at the time. However, he was often troubled in the imperial examinations. Public opinion was dissatisfied, and the examiners paid attention to finding and taking him, but he was lost or missed, and he could not be selected. So he died with his aspirations. Dongyang eventually died without an heir. Zhaoxian loved prostitutes, and Dongyang condemned him. He specially wrote on the door of his residence, "Today Willow Lane, tomorrow Flower Street. Reciting poems and reading books, scholar, scholar!" Zhaoxian returned, saw it, and immediately continued to write, "Today's heavy rain, tomorrow's strong wind. Harmonizing Yin and Yang, Prime Minister, Prime Minister!" Others, such as Gong Banlun of the Qing Dynasty towards his father Ding'an, and Guo Zhuoying towards his father Songtao, one used paint to smear his books after death, and knocked on his wooden tablet with a pen, and the other used a 100-point assessment method and only gave his father's ancient articles 50 points. These are all examples of fathers and sons who were both literary men and despised each other.

Someone said to me, the reason why today's literary men despise each other is different from the past. Because in today's world, there is nothing to say, only humor! I don't know if it's true, I will ask the great humorist Mr. Lin Yutang.

Correction of "Empty-Handed" 279

— Feng Zhiyu

When I wrote "Empty-Handed" a few days ago, I didn't have a book at hand. When it came to the part of "Yan's Family Instructions," I only relied on my memory. Later, I was afraid of making mistakes, so I tried to find the original book to check it, and found that I had made a mistake in my description of Yan Zhitui. His "Teaching Sons" chapter says丨

"During the Qi Dynasty, there was a scholar-official who once said to me: I have a son who is seventeen years old and knows a little about writing. I taught him the Xianbei language and playing the pipa, and he is somewhat knowledgeable. If he uses this to serve the nobles and ministers, he will be loved by everyone, and it is also important." I bowed my head and did not answer at that time. How strange is this son's teaching of his son. If he achieves the position of Prime Minister through this profession, I would not want you to do it."

Then the Qi scholar's method is the method of officials, merchants, gentlemen and gentry after the Gengzi year. Mr. Shi Zhicun is a combination of the two archetypes of the Qi scholar and Yan Zhitui, and it is also the method of some people now, which can be renamed "Northern Dynasty style morality," and it is still a serious social problem.

I should be very sorry to Mr. Yan, but he has already died, and it doesn't matter whether I apologize or not. Now I am only correcting my mistakes to Mr. Shi and the readers here.

A Mistake by Mr. Gao Ming 280

— Ju Sheng

The "Free Talk" on the 17th contained an article entitled "A Record of Watching Roaring in Tokyo" signed "Gao Ming." It said: "That night, two plays were performed, one of which was Jiang Kouhuan's "Opium War." "This play was later renamed "The First European Flag" and has been translated into Chinese by a certain gentleman." But as far as I know, "Opium War" was written by Murayama Tomoyoshi and was translated last year by Yuan Shu, who was transformed from Yuan Xueyi and Yuan Xiaoyi into the current Yuan Xiaoyi, and was published by Hufeng Bookstore.

Two Brothers (10) 281

— Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

"What did he say, this gentleman?"

"He said that Mr. Lecaru would come here in person tonight."

Mr. Lecaru was a notary who had dealings with Old Man Roland, and also a friend of sorts. Since he had someone notify in advance that he would come to visit in the evening, there must be some urgent and important matter; so the four members of the Roland family looked at each other, and like all people with meager family property who were afraid of having dealings with a notary, everyone was disturbed by this news. Because in their minds, the name of a notary would make people think of terms, inheritance, lawsuits, and a whole bunch of pleasant or terrible things. After a few seconds of silence, the father murmured:

"What's going on?"

Mrs. Lu laughed:

"Don't think about it, it must be a matter of inheritance. I believe it must be, I am a lucky star."

But they had never hoped that anyone would leave them anything after death.

Grandma Roland, who had a very good memory of blood relations, immediately searched her own and her husband's relatives in her mind, tracing the parent-child relationship from generation to generation, and tracing the branches of the cousin relationship.

She didn't even take off her hat and asked:

"Hey, Dad, (she calls her husband "Dad" at home, and sometimes calls "Mr. Roland" in front of guests,) hey, Dad, do you remember who Joseph Lebrun's second wife was?"

"I remember, a girl named Dumeny, the daughter of a paper shop owner."

"Did he have children?"

"I remember there were, at least four or five."

"That's not right, then there won't be anything in this area."

She was already enthusiastically engaged in this search, eager for a small fortune to fall on them from the sky. Bill was very fond of his mother. He knew that his mother liked to daydream a little, and he was afraid that if the news was not good but bad, it would disappoint his mother and make her feel a little pain and a little sadness. He stopped her and said:

"Mom, don't be too enthusiastic. There won't be any more American uncles like that. I think, nine times out of ten"

"It's coming to propose marriage to Jian."

Everyone was a little surprised to hear this, and Jian was even more angry that his brother had said this in front of Mrs. Lu.

"Why is it proposing marriage to me and not to you? This assumption is very debatable. You are the eldest son; others"

"Will think of you first. Besides, I, I don't want to get married."

Bill mocked him:

"Then are you already someone's lover?"

The other was very unhappy and replied:

"Do you have to be someone's lover to say that you don't want to get married?"

"Ah! That's right, the word "yet" corrects everything; you are waiting."

"Whatever you want, just say I'm waiting."

But Old Man Roland listened to their words, thought for a while, and suddenly came to the most plausible conclusion:

"Okay! We are so stupid to think about it like this. Mr. Lecaru is our friend. He knows Bill is looking for"

"A clinic, and Jian is looking for a law firm. He must have seen some place that suits the needs of one of you two."

This matter was so simple and possible that everyone agreed.

"Dinner is ready," said the maid.

So everyone went back to their rooms to wash their hands before sitting down at the table. (To be continued)

Talking Points

Talking about "National X" 282

— Lizhai

In our old nation, the application of the word "national" is the most widespread and almost "department store"-like.

Since the opening of the sea ban and the arrival of foreigners from the East, some progressive scholars and officials who were making a fuss about "Westernization" and "Renovation" during the "Xianfeng and Tongzhi periods," a group of stubborn conservatives carried out the word "national quintessence" as a weapon of resistance. This "national quintessence," on the one hand, is all-encompassing for "national goods civilization," and on the other hand, it is the originator of all "Tu X."

Since the abolition of the imperial examination and the opening of schools, up to now, the first item listed as a compulsory course in various schools is our country's "national language," which is so profound and has no scope that many old scholars and pedants with white hair only touch the threshold in the years of "ear-shun" and "ancient hope," and cannot be said to "enter the hall and enter the room."

As the sum of Chinese academic thought that has not been collated, "Sage Kang" and "Madman Zhang" are the most skilled, and Sage Liang and Dr. Hu are also not bad, it is our country's "top-notch" "national studies."

Hospitals have been established one after another, and "doctors" have become more and more popular. What "subcutaneous injection" and "X-ray" have become "unclear." Therefore, "national goods doctors" who take "looking, smelling, asking, and cutting" as the procedure and "liver wood khắc spleen soil" as the classic have risen up to defend themselves, carrying out the big signboard opposite Western medicine: "national medicine." In connection with this, also making a big fuss about its "distilled water" and "scientification" is the "national pharmacy" that "follows the ancient method" of grass roots and tree bark.

Some "old heroes" who "followed the Prime Minister for decades" once "lost their souls," and lowered the flag at half-mast, calling on the officials and the governed to hold the coffin. First, they allocate a batch of people's fat and people's cream to "handle the funeral," and then they allocate a batch of national treasury to repair the Huabiao, tomb passages, and Wengzhong. This set of formulas is called "national funeral." Some "national funerals" are actually heavily discounted and can only be regarded as "official funerals."

When our nation encounters disputes and confrontations, and adds each other with vicious words, it often uses the sexual organs involving the mother, aunt, wife, and younger sister as the center of attack. is A 　jian　's old 　　a hundred "national horses" that were occasionally obtained in his youth.

Plum has five petals, symbolizing the five powers, five courts, and five races. Therefore, it is given the title "national flower" However, since the September 18th Incident, the "friendly country" has discounted the five races by 20% for us, becoming "four joys," so whether the "national flower" continues to belong to plum seems to be still under consideration.

The process of recording time according to the stems and branches, five elements, four seasons, and eight festivals is the "Tu calendar" that Wu Jianguang, Yan Fusun, Xu Suichu, and all the merchants who hope and believe in it must leave and develop separately, and it is now beginning to be sold again.

Mr. Confucius the Second "doesn't know in March," only eats and does nothing, takes being slaughtered as an inevitable destination, and is the most adept at "non-resistance doctrine." It is the "national animal" that the publication of the master of humor has given the title to.

The "friendly country" of the East continues to expand their "lifeline" to the West, and we continue to lose divisions and land, making the ancient objects move south and the people uneasy. This unfinished history is the "national crisis" that everyone knows.

Since the country is in distress, how can we not save it? Therefore, all "XX save the country" have become a situation where programs are mixed and each does its "best." However, the most dominant and promoted by some big bellies is still the saying that "starting from saving the leaky chalice" is the most "modern." Therefore, it has become a trend for a while recently, and it is filling the pockets of many "patriotic people," that is, "national goods."

The little turtles that are displayed in the Chinese Pavilion of the Chicago Expo by several compatriots with "rich national spirit" as "national goods" and sold for four US dollars each can be named "national turtles"!

Many "writers" with solitary loyalty and public anger use them as raw materials for manuscript fees, write them in poems, and write them in articles. Thousands of calls are still not seen, and their form is vague, that is, "national soul."

As the most popular proposition for saving the country, recently, it has also used the "modern ring competition" of "national examination" to select talents, that is, "national art."

"National art to save the country" is almost the rearguard of a large number of "XX to save the country." But if "national art" can no longer save the country, and the Eight Immortals Sword and Tai Chi Quan finally cannot defeat the "friendly country's" airplanes and cannons, then it will be very bad. Maybe Lingzhi Honjo Shigeto and his like will be like Shi Jin, and expand the "lifeline to the hinterland from the border." At that time, all "　　　"　　　、　　 also learn some time changes、　　 two times, 　　　○"!

Once "National ○" is realized, the public of Ah Dou will also inevitably follow the "transformation," and abolish all the titles of "Oldest," "Third," "Seventh," and "Ninth," all of which will be counted as "ranked fourth," and collectively called "China A-Si"!

A Dancing Girl's Life 283

— Jing Jia

The telephone rang. It was two o'clock in the afternoon. Sunlight shone on the foot of the east wall.

The maid picked up the receiver and held it to her ear, "Miss? Miss hasn't gotten up yet!"

Just then, Miss Tao woke up. She yawned in bed.

"Who? Who's calling?" she asked lazily.

"The manager, sir."

"Move the phone to the bedside!" she commanded, and the maid expertly followed the order.

"Who? Oh, Mr. Wang? Good morning, I just woke up. What's the matter? ... Okay, I'll definitely be there a little earlier. Who? Little Chen? Where is he? I don't care. That's fine too. Yes, right. Right. Goodbye."

Miss Tao was about to hang up when she suddenly remembered something and quickly put the receiver to her ear.

"Hello, Mr. Wang, please tell Little Chen, don't let tonight be like last time. Otherwise, I won't stand for it... Hahahaha. Goodbye!"

She lazily hung up the phone and stretched. She sat up.

An hour later, she finally finished washing up. After eating her breakfast, the clock struck four.

She picked up the phone and dialed a number.

"Who? Please ask Mr. Wu to answer the phone... Oh, is that you, Old Wu? Yes, I just got up. How about dinner at the New Asia tonight? ... What, you're not going? Why? ... Headache? I don't care. You're definitely not going? ... Okay, don't bother with me from now on."

She angrily hung up the phone. Just as she was about to turn around, the phone rang again. She picked it up furiously.

"Who?" she shouted.

"Little Chen? What's up? I'm not going, I have a bit of a headache. Yes, a headache. I'm not putting on airs, you misunderstood. ... I really can't go. Look, my voice is even trembling!... "

The maid walked in, "Miss, Mr. Wu is here."

Miss Tao hung up the phone and walked into the living room.

"What a temper, I said something jokingly and you took it seriously!" Mr. Wu said with a smile.

"You rascal!" Miss Tao buried her head in his arms.

"You should go to the dance hall tonight. It's a grand tea dance today!"

"Of course. I'll dance with you. You're not allowed to dance with anyone else."

"That won't do, Little Chen will make a fuss."

"It doesn't matter. Otherwise, you have to take a day off and spend the whole day playing with me."

"Don't be shameless!" She grabbed his beard.

"Don't grab my beard! It hurts! You're such a child."

"You're an old child."

"Haha!" Old Wu laughed, "Really, why are you always clinging to me, an old child?"

"Don't you say that!"

"Hahahaha!"

"This cheongsam doesn't look good anymore!" she said softly.

"Go buy one!"

"It's time to eat too!" she said, "I'll be half-dead tonight!"

"Okay, let's go buy some fabric first!"

"Mmm."

So they went out and got in the car.

In the evening, she danced with Old Wu. Later, she danced with Little Chen again. While dancing, Little Chen whispered to her, "Do you love me or not?"

"I love you and I love him," she said with a smile.

"Why is that?"

"I love you for your face. I love him for his money."

The east dawned, and she took her tired body home.

After Reading "A Review of Vases and Vase Stands" 284

— Hua

The other day, I read Mr. Jing Jia's "A Review of Vases and Vase Stands" in the Spring and Autumn column of this newspaper, criticizing my work "Flowers or Vase Stands?" as being somewhat unnatural. However, after reading Mr. Jing Jia's masterpiece, I am also very dissatisfied with Mr. Jing Jia's views and feel that there are inconsistencies, so I cannot help but come out to explain.

Mr. Jing Jia has already admitted that the term "vase" contains a lot of insulting elements. I think he should know that insult is something that everyone is unwilling to accept. Should we women endure the widespread insult of the term "vase"? He also said that the person who came up with this term only feels embarrassed, inferior, and self-deprecating.

But I can say that the opposite is true. The person who came up with that term is probably ecstatic and receiving praise. Didn't Mr. Jing Jia also admit from the beginning that in recent years "vase" has become a common term for women with professions? If your ideas are echoed by the public, wouldn't that be a very joyful thing? What is there to be embarrassed about? Indeed, true gold is not afraid of fire, but I cannot deny that there is absolutely no fake gold mixed in with professional women, and professional men are not purely true gold either.

As for the term "vase stand," my views are also completely different from Mr. Jing Jia's explanation. Mr. Jing Jia's explanation is that the vase is elevated by the stand, so he says that women must rely on men to enhance everything about women, but my original intention is that modern female employees in companies and organizations are ornaments and are called "vases." Aren't modern male employees in companies and organizations also ornaments? Since ornamental female employees have already been called "vases," then ornamental male employees are naturally either "flowers" or "vase stands." The "vase stand" is precisely what the "vase" steps on, because there are not a few modern male employees who willingly prostrate themselves under the feet of modern female employees to serve them!

As for saying that people with self-respect would never apply these terms to others, this sounds very right, but unfortunately, people nowadays don't have the same understanding and reason as Mr. Jing Jia. Otherwise, the term "vase" would not have become so widespread that even Mr. Jing Jia cannot help but admit that it has become a common term for women with professions.

Indeed, society needs mutual assistance and cannot be established unilaterally by men or women, but when gender equality is just beginning and women's professions are just sprouting, how can we allow others to destroy them so widely? We can disdain the contemptible creatures who came up with this term, but there are so many people who blindly follow him that almost all professional women in the country are affected by him. Should we women forever embrace a policy of non-resistance?

Drama

War and Peace (55) (A Four-Act Play) 287

— Ling He

Act IV: Where to Go? Scene 1

Security Team Member A: Heavens, my god, what's going to happen? Third Master Zhou, we're finished now.

Village Chief: Help!

Security Team Member B: What's the use of shouting like that? Who's going to come and save you?

Village Chief: If I had known this, we should have left with that team of soldiers.

Security Team Member A: But I think it's okay. It must be the Japanese soldiers fighting the Volunteer Army now. When the Japanese soldiers win, they will come back to save us. Let's wait.

Security Team Member B: What are you talking about? What if the Japanese soldiers are defeated? Are we just going to wait here to die?

Village Chief: Don't be ridiculous, the Japanese soldiers won't be defeated.

Security Team Member B: In any case, we can't just wait here. Let's all think of a way to untie the ropes and leave. Third Master, you untie mine first. Then I'll untie yours.

Village Chief: I won't do that. If I untie you and you run away, who am I going to look for?

Security Team Member A: That's right, if you run away alone, then we're really out of luck.

Security Team Member B: Hey! You guys are really... Okay, Third Master, I'll trust you. I'll untie you first. I'm not afraid of you running away.

(Security Team Member B gets close to the Village Chief. The Young Man appears from behind the tree at this time, watches for a long time, and gently approaches them, kicking Security Team Member B to the ground.)

Young Man: You bastard, still trying to escape?

(The Village Chief sees the Young Man and is shocked.)

Young Man: Oh? You're here? What's up? Haha, I didn't expect I'd see you again. Do you recognize me? (Slaps him) You bastard! Now you've run into my hands. Do you still want to collect taxes? (Someone blows a gathering horn in the distance)

Village Chief: Big Brother Monk, thank you, spare me this time.

Young Man: Spare you? Okay. Come on! (To inside) Come and see our village chief worshiping the sky.

(Many Volunteer Army soldiers capture a Japanese prisoner of war, followed by several people who were captured by the Japanese soldiers.)

Security Team Member A: Hey! Why are they back? Did the Japanese soldiers release them?

Village Chief: Don't make a sound! (Trembling) We're finished now that we've run into the Volunteer Army.

Security Team Member B: Is that right? So the Japanese soldiers were defeated after all.

Platoon Leader: (Seeing the Village Chief and them) Hey! Who are these people?

Young Man: This is our village chief. He usually does too many good deeds, so everyone has tied him up.

Platoon Leader: Bah! Damned thing.

Soldier A: Damn it, this time it's really satisfying.

Young Man B: What exactly happened? How did they wipe out more than a hundred people all at once?

Soldier B: Don't you know? We ambushed on both sides of the mountain at the gate. We knew the Japanese soldiers would definitely go there, so we used explosives to blow up the mountain. The rocks and wood all rolled down. We were afraid they wouldn't die?

Young Man: Platoon Leader, what do you think we should do with these traitors?

Platoon Leader: Isn't that easy? Take them to the rice field over there and let the villagers judge them.

Young Man C: That's great, come on, let's take them over there. Today, we can finally vent our anger!

Village Chief: (To the Platoon Leader) Sir, save our lives!

Platoon Leader: Bah, to hell with you. (Everyone laughs.) (The Young Men pull the Village Chief and the other two away.) Hey, now let's interrogate that prisoner of war. How exactly did he get captured?
